It be a teacher 's duty to find and develop it .
That be what our School Management professor at Queen 's tell u , you know .
Do you suppose you could find any good in a child by whip him ?
It 's far more important to influence the child aright than it be even to teach them the three R 's , Professor Rennie say . ''
`` But the Inspector examine them in the three R 's , mind you , and he wo n't give you a good report if they do n't come up to his standard , '' protest Jane .
`` I 'd rather have my pupil love me and look back to me in after year a a real helper than be on the roll of honor , '' assert Anne decidedly .
`` Would n't you punish child at all , when they misbehave ? ''
ask Gilbert .
`` Oh , yes , I suppose I shall have to , although I know I 'll hate to do it .
But you can keep them in at recess or stand them on the floor or give them line to write . ''
`` I suppose you wo n't punish the girl by make them sit with the boy ? ''
say Jane slyly .
Gilbert and Anne look at each other and smile rather foolishly .
Once upon a time , Anne have be make to sit with Gilbert for punishment and sad and bitter have be the consequence thereof .
`` Well , time will tell which be the best way , '' say Jane philosophically a they part .

She walk slowly , enjoy the sweetness of wood and field and the starry summer twilight , and think soberly about the new duty she be to take up on the morrow .

This be not the first time Anne have run over and chat with Mr. Harrison since the notable affair of the Jersey cow .
She have be there several evening and Mr. Harrison and she be very good friend , although there be time and season when Anne find the outspokenness on which he pride himself rather try .

He certainly never pay her any to her face .

be his greeting a Anne come up the veranda step .
`` No , indeed , '' say Anne indignantly .
She be an excellent target for teasing because she always take thing so seriously .
`` I shall never have a switch in my school , Mr. Harrison .
Of course , I shall have to have a pointer , but I shall use it for point ONLY . ''
`` So you mean to strap them instead ?
Well , I do n't know but you 're right .
A switch sting more at the time but the strap smart longer , that 's a fact . ''
`` I shall not use anything of the sort .
I 'm not go to whip my pupil . ''
`` Bless my soul , '' exclaim Mr. Harrison in genuine astonishment , `` how do you lay out to keep order then ? ''
`` I shall govern by affection , Mr. Harrison . ''
`` It wo n't do , '' say Mr. Harrison , `` wo n't do at all , Anne .
` Spare the rod and spoil the child . '
When I go to school the master whip me regular every day because he say if I be n't in mischief just then I be plot it . ''
`` Methods have change since your schooldays , Mr. Harrison . ''
`` But human nature have n't .
Mark my word , you 'll never manage the young fry unless you keep a rod in pickle for them .
The thing be impossible . ''
`` Well , I 'm go to try my way first , '' say Anne , who have a fairly strong will of her own and be apt to cling very tenaciously to her theory .
`` You 're pretty stubborn , I reckon , '' be Mr. Harrison 's way of put it .
`` Well , well , we 'll see .
Someday when you get rile up ... and people with hair like yours be desperate apt to get riled ... you 'll forget all your pretty little notion and give some of them a whaling .
You 're too young to be teach anyhow ... far too young and childish . ''
Altogether , Anne go to bed that night in a rather pessimistic mood .
She sleep poorly and be so pale and tragic at breakfast next morning that Marilla be alarm and insist on make her take a cup of scorch ginger tea .
Anne sip it patiently , although she could not imagine what good ginger tea would do .
Had it be some magic brew , potent to confer age and experience , Anne would have swallow a quart of it without flinch .
`` Marilla , what if I fail ! ''
`` You 'll hardly fail completely in one day and there 's plenty more day come , '' say Marilla .
`` The trouble with you , Anne , be that you 'll expect to teach those child everything and reform all their fault right off , and if you ca n't you 'll think you 've fail . ''
V A Full-fledged Schoolma'am When Anne reach the school that morning ... for the first time in her life she have traverse the Birch Path deaf and blind to it beauty ... all be quiet and still .

She hang up her hat and face her pupil , hop that she do not look a frightened and foolish a she felt and that they would not perceive how she be tremble .
She have sit up until nearly twelve the precede night compose a speech she mean to make to her pupil upon open the school .
She have revise and improve it painstakingly , and then she have learn it off by heart .
It be a very good speech and have some very fine idea in it , especially about mutual help and earnest striving after knowledge .
The only trouble be that she could not now remember a word of it .
After what seem to her a year ... about ten second in reality ... she say faintly , `` Take your Testaments , please , '' and sink breathlessly into her chair under cover of the rustle and clatter of desk lid that follow .
While the child read their verse Anne marshal her shaky wit into order and look over the array of little pilgrim to the Grownup Land .
Most of them be , of course , quite well know to her .

Anne secretly felt more interest in these ten than in those whose possibility be already fairly well map out to her .

It be a thrilling idea .

A tall , awkward girl in a back seat , who seem to have too many foot and hand , Anne could not place at all , but later on discover that her name be Barbara Shaw and that she have come to live with an Avonlea aunt .

But when Anne 's eye meet those of the boy at the front desk face her own , a queer little thrill go over her , a if she have find her genius .
She know this must be Paul Irving and that Mrs. Rachel Lynde have be right for once when she prophesy that he would be unlike the Avonlea child .

She know Paul be ten but he look no more than eight .

His mouth be delicious , be full without pout , the crimson lip just softly touch and curve into finely finish little corner that narrowly escape be dimple .

And how terrible it would be to be do something you do n't like every day for ... well , say forty year .
Anne be of two mind whether to have her cry out then and there , or wait till she be safely in her own white room at home .

Now , Miss Shirley , the correct pronunciation of our name be DonNELL ... accent on the last syllable .
I hope you 'll remember this in future . ''

`` That boy have such plebeian taste , Miss Shirley .

I yield , because Uncle Jacob be a rich old bachelor .
And what do you think , Miss Shirley ?
When our innocent boy be five year old Uncle Jacob actually go and get marry and now he have three boy of his own .

From that day I call my son St. Clair and St. Clair I be determine he shall be call .
His father obstinately continue to call him Jacob , and the boy himself have a perfectly unaccountable preference for the vulgar name .
But St. Clair he be and St. Clair he shall remain .
You will kindly remember this , Miss Shirley , will you not ?
THANK you .

Donnell ... accent on the last syllable ... and St. Clair ... on no account Jacob .
You 'll remember ?
THANK you . ''

VI All Sorts and Conditions of Men ... and woman A September day on Prince Edward Island hill ; a crisp wind blow up over the sand dune from the sea ; a long red road , wind through field and wood , now loop itself about a corner of thick set spruce , now thread a plantation of young maple with great feathery sheet of fern beneath them , now dip down into a hollow where a brook flash out of the wood and into them again , now bask in open sunshine between ribbon of golden-rod and smoke-blue aster ; air athrill with the piping of myriad of cricket , those glad little pensioner of the summer hill ; a plump brown pony amble along the road ; two girl behind him , full to the lip with the simple , priceless joy of youth and life .
`` Oh , this be a day leave over from Eden , be n't it , Diana ? ''
... and Anne sigh for sheer happiness .
`` The air have magic in it .
Look at the purple in the cup of the harvest valley , Diana .
And oh , do smell the die fir !
It 's come up from that little sunny hollow where Mr. Eben Wright have be cut fence pole .
Bliss be it on such a day to be alive ; but to smell die fir be very heaven .
That 's two third Wordsworth and one third Anne Shirley .
It do n't seem possible that there should be die fir in heaven , do it ?
And yet it do n't seem to me that heaven would be quite perfect if you could n't get a whiff of dead fir a you go through it wood .
Perhaps we 'll have the odor there without the death .
Yes , I think that will be the way .
That delicious aroma must be the soul of the fir ... and of course it will be just souls in heaven . ''
`` Trees have n't souls , '' say practical Diana , `` but the smell of dead fir be certainly lovely .
I 'm go to make a cushion and fill it with fir needle .
You 'd better make one too , Anne . ''
`` I think I shall ... and use it for my nap .
I 'd be certain to dream I be a dryad or a woodnymph then .
But just this minute I 'm well content to be Anne Shirley , Avonlea schoolma'am , drive over a road like this on such a sweet , friendly day . ''
`` It 's a lovely day but we have anything but a lovely task before u , '' sigh Diana .
`` Why on earth do you offer to canvas this road , Anne ?

`` That be why I choose it .

I 'm sorry on your account ; but you need n't say a word at the cranky place .
I 'll do all the talk ... Mrs. Lynde would say I be well able to .
Mrs. Lynde do n't know whether to approve of our enterprise or not .
She incline to , when she remember that Mr. and Mrs. Allan be in favor of it ; but the fact that village improvement society first originate in the States be a count against it .
So she be halt between two opinion and only success will justify u in Mrs. Lynde 's eye .

I shall never forget the thrill it give me when I find out that Mrs. Charlotte E. Morgan be Priscilla 's aunt .

`` In Toronto .
And Priscilla say she be come to the Island for a visit next summer , and if it be possible Priscilla be go to arrange to have u meet her .
That seem almost too good to be true -- but it 's something pleasant to imagine after you go to bed . ''
The Avonlea Village Improvement Society be an organize fact .
Gilbert Blythe be president , Fred Wright vice-president , Anne Shirley secretary , and Diana Barry treasurer .
The `` Improvers , '' a they be promptly christen , be to meet once a fortnight at the home of the member .
It be admit that they could not expect to affect many improvement so late in the season ; but they mean to plan the next summer 's campaign , collect and discus idea , write and read paper , and , a Anne say , educate the public sentiment generally .
There be some disapproval , of course , and ... which the Improvers felt much more keenly ... a good deal of ridicule .
Mr. Elisha Wright be report to have say that a more appropriate name for the organization would be Courting Club .
Mrs. Hiram Sloane declare she have hear the Improvers mean to plough up all the roadside and set them out with geranium .
Mr. Levi Boulter warn his neighbor that the Improvers would insist that everybody pull down his house and rebuild it after plan approve by the society .
Mr. James Spencer send them word that he wish they would kindly shovel down the church hill .
Eben Wright tell Anne that he wish the Improvers could induce old Josiah Sloane to keep his whisker trim .
Mr. Lawrence Bell say he would whitewash his barn if nothing else would please them but he would NOT hang lace curtain in the cowstable window .
Mr. Major Spencer ask Clifton Sloane , an Improver who drive the milk to the Carmody cheese factory , if it be true that everybody would have to have his milk-stand hand-painted next summer and keep an embroidered centerpiece on it .
In spite of ... or perhaps , human nature be what it be , because of ... this , the Society go gamely to work at the only improvement they could hope to bring about that fall .
At the second meeting , in the Barry parlor , Oliver Sloane move that they start a subscription to re-shingle and paint the hall ; Julia Bell second it , with an uneasy feeling that she be do something not exactly ladylike .

They drive to the end of the road and canvassed homeward , call first on the `` Andrew girl . ''

Eliza be there ... very much so ... and look even grim than usual .
Miss Eliza be one of those people who give you the impression that life be indeed a vale of tear , and that a smile , never to speak of a laugh , be a waste of nervous energy truly reprehensible .
The Andrew girl have be `` girl '' for fifty odd year and seem likely to remain girl to the end of their earthly pilgrimage .
Catherine , it be say , have not entirely give up hope , but Eliza , who be bear a pessimist , have never have any .
They live in a little brown house build in a sunny corner scoop out of Mark Andrew 's beech wood .

It 's no benefit to the settlement ... just a place for young folk to meet and carry on when they 's good be home in their bed . ''

`` I do n't see the necessity .

Miss Eliza 's voice express the utmost contempt .
`` It do n't signify what you THINK , Catherine Andrews .
Facts be fact . ''

plead Anne .

He do n't seem to be in his proper sphere at all .
I have hear of henpecked husband and now I felt that I saw one .
It be on my lip to say , ` Mr. Blair , if you 'll give u a subscription for the hall I 'll mix up your cake for you . '
But I suddenly think it would n't be neighborly to drive too sharp a bargain with a fellow creature in distress .
So I offer to mix the cake for him without any condition at all .
He just jump at my offer .
He say he 'd be use to make his own bread before he be marry but he fear cake be beyond him , and yet he hat to disappoint his wife .
He get me another apron , and Diana beat the egg and I mix the cake .
Mr. Blair run about and get u the material .
He have forget all about his apron and when he run it stream out behind him and Diana say she think she would die to see it .
He say he could bake the cake all right ... he be use to that ... and then he ask for our list and he put down four dollar .
So you see we be reward .
But even if he have n't give a cent I 'd always feel that we have do a truly Christian act in help him . ''
Theodore White 's be the next stopping place .
Neither Anne nor Diana have ever be there before , and they have only a very slight acquaintance with Mrs. Theodore , who be not give to hospitality .
Should they go to the back or front door ?
While they hold a whispered consultation Mrs. Theodore appear at the front door with an armful of newspaper .
Deliberately she lay them down one by one on the porch floor and the porch step , and then down the path to the very foot of her mystified caller .
`` Will you please wipe your foot carefully on the grass and then walk on these paper ? ''
she say anxiously .
`` I 've just sweep the house all over and I ca n't have any more dust track in .
The path 's be real muddy since the rain yesterday . ''
`` Do n't you dare laugh , '' warn Anne in a whisper , a they march along the newspaper .
`` And I implore you , Diana , not to look at me , no matter what she say , or I shall not be able to keep a sober face . ''
The paper extend across the hall and into a prim , fleckless parlor .
Anne and Diana sit down gingerly on the near chair and explain their errand .
Mrs. White hear them politely , interrupt only twice , once to chase out an adventurous fly , and once to pick up a tiny wisp of grass that have fall on the carpet from Anne 's dress .
Anne felt wretchedly guilty ; but Mrs. White subscribe two dollar and pay the money down ... `` to prevent u from have to go back for it , '' Diana say when they get away .
Mrs. White have the newspaper gather up before they have their horse untied and a they drive out of the yard they saw her busily wield a broom in the hall .
`` I 've always hear that Mrs. Theodore White be the neat woman alive and I 'll believe it after this , '' say Diana , give way to her suppressed laughter as soon a it be safe .
`` I be glad she have no child , '' say Anne solemnly .
`` It would be dreadful beyond word for them if she have . ''
At the Spencers ' Mrs. Isabella Spencer make them miserable by say something ill-natured about everyone in Avonlea .
Mr. Thomas Boulter refuse to give anything because the hall , when it have be build , twenty year before , have n't be build on the site he recommend .
Mrs. Esther Bell , who be the picture of health , take half an hour to detail all her ache and pain , and sadly put down fifty cent because she would n't be there that time next year to do it ... no , she would be in her grave .
Their bad reception , however , be at Simon Fletcher 's .
When they drive into the yard they saw two face peer at them through the porch window .
But although they rap and wait patiently and persistently nobody come to the door .
Two decidedly ruffle and indignant girl drive away from Simon Fletcher 's .
Even Anne admit that she be begin to feel discourage .
But the tide turn after that .
Several Sloane homestead come next , where they get liberal subscription , and from that to the end they fare well , with only an occasional snub .
Their last place of call be at Robert Dickson 's by the pond bridge .
They stay to tea here , although they be nearly home , rather than risk offend Mrs. Dickson , who have the reputation of be a very `` touchy '' woman .
While they be there old Mrs. James White call in .
`` I 've just be down to Lorenzo 's , '' she announce .
`` He 's the proudest man in Avonlea this minute .
What do you think ?
There 's a brand new boy there ... and after seven girl that 's quite an event , I can tell you . ''
Anne prick up her ear , and when they drive away she say .
`` I 'm go straight to Lorenzo White 's . ''
`` But he live on the White Sands road and it 's quite a distance out of our way , '' protest Diana .
`` Gilbert and Fred will canvas him . ''
`` They be not go around until next Saturday and it will be too late by then , '' say Anne firmly .
`` The novelty will be wear off .
Lorenzo White be dreadfully mean but he will subscribe to ANYTHING just now .
We must n't let such a golden opportunity slip , Diana . ''
The result justify Anne 's foresight .
Mr. White meet them in the yard , beam like the sun upon an Easter day .
When Anne ask for a subscription he agree enthusiastically .
`` Certain , certain .
Just put me down for a dollar more than the high subscription you 've get . ''
`` That will be five dollar ... Mr. Daniel Blair put down four , '' say Anne , half afraid .
But Lorenzo do not flinch .
`` Five it be ... and here 's the money on the spot .
Now , I want you to come into the house .
There 's something in there worth see ... something very few people have see a yet .
Just come in and pass YOUR opinion . ''
`` What will we say if the baby be n't pretty ? ''
whisper Diana in trepidation a they follow the excited Lorenzo into the house .
`` Oh , there will certainly be something else nice to say about it , '' say Anne easily .
`` There always be about a baby . ''
The baby WAS pretty , however , and Mr. White felt that he get his five dollar ' worth of the girl ' honest delight over the plump little newcomer .
But that be the first , last , and only time that Lorenzo White ever subscribe to anything .
Anne , tire a she be , make one more effort for the public weal that night , slip over the field to interview Mr. Harrison , who be a usual smoke his pipe on the veranda with Ginger beside him .
Strickly speak he be on the Carmody road ; but Jane and Gertie , who be not acquaint with him save by doubtful report , have nervously beg Anne to canvas him .
Mr. Harrison , however , flatly refuse to subscribe a cent , and all Anne 's wile be in vain .
`` But I think you approve of our society , Mr. Harrison , '' she mourn .
`` So I do ... so I do ... but my approval do n't go as deep a my pocket , Anne . ''
`` A few more experience such a I have have today would make me a much of a pessimist a Miss Eliza Andrews , '' Anne tell her reflection in the east gable mirror at bedtime .
VII The Pointing of Duty Anne lean back in her chair one mild October evening and sigh .
She be sit at a table cover with text book and exercise , but the closely write sheet of paper before her have no apparent connection with study or school work .
`` What be the matter ? ''
ask Gilbert , who have arrive at the open kitchen door just in time to hear the sigh .
Anne color , and thrust her write out of sight under some school composition .
`` Nothing very dreadful .
I be just try to write out some of my thought , a Professor Hamilton advise me , but I could n't get them to please me .
They seem so still and foolish directly they 're write down on white paper with black ink .
Fancies be like shadow ... you ca n't cage them , they 're such wayward , dance thing .
But perhaps I 'll learn the secret some day if I keep on try .
I have n't a great many spare moment , you know .
By the time I finish correct school exercise and composition , I do n't always feel like write any of my own . ''
`` You be get on splendidly in school , Anne .
All the child like you , '' say Gilbert , sit down on the stone step .
`` No , not all .
Anthony Pye do n't and WO N'T like me .
What be bad , he do n't respect me ... no , he do n't .
He simply hold me in contempt and I do n't mind confess to you that it worry me miserably .
It be n't that he be so very bad ... he be only rather mischievous , but no bad than some of the others .
He seldom disobey me ; but he obey with a scornful air of toleration a if it be n't worthwhile dispute the point or he would ... and it have a bad effect on the others .
I 've try every way to win him but I 'm begin to fear I never shall .
I want to , for he 's rather a cute little lad , if he IS a Pye , and I could like him if he 'd let me . ''
`` Probably it 's merely the effect of what he hear at home . ''
`` Not altogether .
Anthony be an independent little chap and make up his own mind about thing .
He have always go to men before and he say girl teacher be no good .
Well , we 'll see what patience and kindness will do .
I like overcome difficulty and teaching be really very interesting work .
Paul Irving make up for all that be lack in the others .
That child be a perfect darling , Gilbert , and a genius into the bargain .
I 'm persuade the world will hear of him some day , '' conclude Anne in a tone of conviction .
`` I like teach , too , '' say Gilbert .
`` It 's good training , for one thing .
Why , Anne , I 've learn more in the week I 've be teach the young idea of White Sands than I learn in all the year I go to school myself .
We all seem to be get on pretty well .
The Newbridge people like Jane , I hear ; and I think White Sands be tolerably satisfied with your humble servant ... all except Mr. Andrew Spencer .
I meet Mrs. Peter Blewett on my way home last night and she tell me she think it her duty to inform me that Mr. Spencer do n't approve of my method . ''
`` Have you ever notice , '' ask Anne reflectively , `` that when people say it be their duty to tell you a certain thing you may prepare for something disagreeable ?
Why be it that they never seem to think it a duty to tell you the pleasant thing they hear about you ?
Mrs. H. B. DonNELL call at the school again yesterday and tell me she think it HER duty to inform me that Mrs. Harmon Andrew do n't approve of my reading fairy tale to the child , and that Mr. Rogerson think Prillie be n't come on fast enough in arithmetic .
If Prillie would spend less time make eye at the boy over her slate she might do good .
I feel quite sure that Jack Gillis work her class sum for her , though I 've never be able to catch him red-handed . ''
`` Have you succeed in reconcile Mrs. DonNELL 's hopeful son to his saintly name ? ''
`` Yes , '' laugh Anne , `` but it be really a difficult task .
At first , when I call him ` St. Clair ' he would not take the least notice until I 'd speak two or three time ; and then , when the other boy nudge him , he would look up with such an aggrieved air , a if I 'd call him John or Charlie and he could n't be expect to know I mean him .
So I keep him in after school one night and talk kindly to him .
I tell him his mother wish me to call him St. Clair and I could n't go against her wish .
He saw it when it be all explain out ... he 's really a very reasonable little fellow ... and he say I could call him St. Clair but that he 'd ` lick the stuffing ' out of any of the boy that try it .
Of course , I have to rebuke him again for use such shocking language .
Since then I call him St. Clair and the boy call him Jake and all go smoothly .
He inform me that he mean to be a carpenter , but Mrs. DonNELL say I be to make a college professor out of him . ''
The mention of college give a new direction to Gilbert 's thought , and they talk for a time of their plan and wish ... gravely , earnestly , hopefully , a youth love to talk , while the future be yet an untrodden path full of wonderful possibility .
Gilbert have finally make up his mind that he be go to be a doctor .
`` It 's a splendid profession , '' he say enthusiastically .
`` A fellow have to fight something all through life ... do n't somebody once define man a a fight animal ?
... and I want to fight disease and pain and ignorance ... which be all member one of another .
I want to do my share of honest , real work in the world , Anne ... add a little to the sum of human knowledge that all the good men have be accumulate since it begin .
The folk who live before me have do so much for me that I want to show my gratitude by do something for the folk who will live after me .
It seem to me that be the only way a fellow can get square with his obligation to the race . ''
`` I 'd like to add some beauty to life , '' say Anne dreamily .
`` I do n't exactly want to make people KNOW more ... though I know that IS the noble ambition ... but I 'd love to make them have a pleasanter time because of me ... to have some little joy or happy thought that would never have exist if I have n't be bear . ''
`` I think you 're fulfil that ambition every day , '' say Gilbert admiringly .
And he be right .
Anne be one of the child of light by birthright .
After she have pass through a life with a smile or a word throw across it like a gleam of sunshine the owner of that life saw it , for the time be at least , a hopeful and lovely and of good report .
Finally Gilbert rise regretfully .
`` Well , I must run up to MacPhersons ' .
Moody Spurgeon come home from Queen 's today for Sunday and he be to bring me out a book Professor Boyd be lend me . ''
`` And I must get Marilla 's tea .
She go to see Mrs. Keith this evening and she will soon be back . ''
Anne have tea ready when Marilla come home ; the fire be crackle cheerily , a vase of frost-bleached fern and ruby-red maple leaf adorn the table , and delectable odor of ham and toast pervade the air .
But Marilla sink into her chair with a deep sigh .
`` Are your eye trouble you ?
Does your head ache ? ''
query Anne anxiously .
`` No .
I 'm only tired ... and worry .
It 's about Mary and those child ... Mary be bad ... she ca n't last much long .
And a for the twin , I do n't know what be to become of them . ''
`` Has n't their uncle be hear from ? ''
`` Yes , Mary have a letter from him .
He 's work in a lumber camp and ` shack it , ' whatever that mean .
Anyway , he say he ca n't possibly take the child till the spring .
He expect to be marry then and will have a home to take them to ; but he say she must get some of the neighbor to keep them for the winter .
She say she ca n't bear to ask any of them .
Mary never get on any too well with the East Grafton people and that 's a fact .
And the long and short of it be , Anne , that I 'm sure Mary want me to take those child ... she do n't say so but she LOOKED it . ''
`` Oh ! ''
Anne clasp her hand , all athrill with excitement .
`` And of course you will , Marilla , wo n't you ? ''
`` I have n't make up my mind , '' say Marilla rather tartly .
`` I do n't rush into thing in your headlong way , Anne .
Third cousinship be a pretty slim claim .
And it will be a fearful responsibility to have two child of six year to look after ... twin , at that . ''
Marilla have an idea that twin be just twice as bad a single child .
`` Twins be very interesting ... at least one pair of them , '' say Anne .
`` It 's only when there be two or three pair that it get monotonous .
And I think it would be real nice for you to have something to amuse you when I 'm away in school . ''
`` I do n't reckon there 'd be much amusement in it ... more worry and bother than anything else , I should say .
It would n't be so risky if they be even as old a you be when I take you .
I would n't mind Dora so much ... she seem good and quiet .
But that Davy be a limb . ''
Anne be fond of child and her heart yearn over the Keith twin .
The remembrance of her own neglected childhood be very vivid with her still .
She know that Marilla 's only vulnerable point be her stern devotion to what she believe to be her duty , and Anne skillfully marshal her argument along this line .
`` If Davy be naughty it 's all the more reason why he should have good training , be n't it , Marilla ?
If we do n't take them we do n't know who will , nor what kind of influence may surround them .
Suppose Mrs. Keith 's next door neighbor , the Sprotts , be to take them .
Mrs. Lynde say Henry Sprott be the most profane man that ever live and you ca n't believe a word his child say .
Would n't it be dreadful to have the twin learn anything like that ?
Or suppose they go to the Wiggins ' .
Mrs. Lynde say that Mr. Wiggins sell everything off the place that can be sell and bring his family up on skim milk .
You would n't like your relation to be starve , even if they be only third cousin , would you ?
It seem to me , Marilla , that it be our duty to take them . ''
`` I suppose it be , '' assent Marilla gloomily .
`` I daresay I 'll tell Mary I 'll take them .
You need n't look so delighted , Anne .
It will mean a good deal of extra work for you .
I ca n't sew a stitch on account of my eye , so you 'll have to see to the making and mending of their clothes .
And you do n't like sew . ''
`` I hate it , '' say Anne calmly , `` but if you be willing to take those child from a sense of duty surely I can do their sewing from a sense of duty .
It do people good to have to do thing they do n't like ... in moderation . ''
VIII Marilla Adopts Twins Mrs. Rachel Lynde be sit at her kitchen window , knit a quilt , just a she have be sit one even several year previously when Matthew Cuthbert have drive down over the hill with what Mrs. Rachel call `` his import orphan . ''
But that have be in springtime ; and this be late autumn , and all the wood be leafless and the field sere and brown .
The sun be just set with a great deal of purple and golden pomp behind the dark wood west of Avonlea when a buggy drawn by a comfortable brown nag come down the hill .
Mrs. Rachel peer at it eagerly .
`` There 's Marilla get home from the funeral , '' she say to her husband , who be lie on the kitchen lounge .
Thomas Lynde lay more on the lounge nowadays than he have be use to do , but Mrs. Rachel , who be so sharp at notice anything beyond her own household , have not a yet notice this .
`` And she 's get the twin with her , ... yes , there 's Davy leaning over the dashboard grabbing at the pony 's tail and Marilla jerk him back .
Dora 's sit up on the seat as prim a you please .
She always look a if she 'd just be starch and iron .
Well , poor Marilla be go to have her hand full this winter and no mistake .
Still , I do n't see that she could do anything less than take them , under the circumstance , and she 'll have Anne to help her .
Anne 's tickle to death over the whole business , and she have a real knacky way with child , I must say .
Dear me , it do n't seem a day since poor Matthew bring Anne herself home and everybody laugh at the idea of Marilla bring up a child .
And now she have adopt twin .
You 're never safe from be surprise till you 're dead . ''
The fat pony jog over the bridge in Lynde 's Hollow and along the Green Gables lane .
Marilla 's face be rather grim .
It be ten mile from East Grafton and Davy Keith seem to be possess with a passion for perpetual motion .
It be beyond Marilla 's power to make him sit still and she have be in an agony the whole way lest he fall over the back of the wagon and break his neck , or tumble over the dashboard under the pony 's heel .
In despair she finally threaten to whip him soundly when she get him home .
Whereupon Davy climb into her lap , regardless of the rein , fling his chubby arm about her neck and give her a bear-like hug .
`` I do n't believe you mean it , '' he say , smack her wrinkled cheek affectionately .
`` You do n't LOOK like a lady who 'd whip a little boy just 'cause he could n't keep still .
Did n't you find it awful hard to keep still when you be only 's old a me ? ''
`` No , I always keep still when I be tell , '' say Marilla , try to speak sternly , albeit she felt her heart wax soft within her under Davy 's impulsive caress .
`` Well , I s ` pose that be 'cause you be a girl , '' say Davy , squirm back to his place after another hug .
`` You WAS a girl once , I s ` pose , though it 's awful funny to think of it .
Dora can sit still ... but there ai n't much fun in it I do n't think .
Seems to me it must be slow to be a girl .
Here , Dora , let me liven you up a bit . ''
Davy 's method of `` liven up '' be to grasp Dora 's curl in his finger and give them a tug .
Dora shriek and then cry .
`` How can you be such a naughty boy and your poor mother just lay in her grave this very day ? ''
demand Marilla despairingly .
`` But she be glad to die , '' say Davy confidentially .
`` I know , 'cause she tell me so .
She be awful tired of be sick .
We 'd a long talk the night before she die .
She tell me you be go to take me and Dora for the winter and I be to be a good boy .
I 'm go to be good , but ca n't you be good run round just as well a sit still ?
And she say I be always to be kind to Dora and stand up for her , and I 'm go to . ''
`` Do you call pull her hair be kind to her ? ''
`` Well , I ai n't go to let anybody else pull it , '' say Davy , double up his fist and frowning .
`` They 'd just well try it .
I do n't hurt her much ... she just cry 'cause she 's a girl .
I 'm glad I 'm a boy but I 'm sorry I 'm a twin .
When Jimmy Sprott 's sister conterdicks him he just say , ` I 'm oldern you , so of course I know well , ' and that settle HER .
But I ca n't tell Dora that , and she just go on think diffrunt from me .
You might let me drive the gee-gee for a spell , since I 'm a man . ''
Altogether , Marilla be a thankful woman when she drive into her own yard , where the wind of the autumn night be dance with the brown leaf .
Anne be at the gate to meet them and lift the twin out .
Dora submit calmly to be kiss , but Davy respond to Anne 's welcome with one of his hearty hug and the cheerful announcement , `` I 'm Mr. Davy Keith . ''
At the supper table Dora behave like a little lady , but Davy 's manner leave much to be desire .
`` I 'm so hungry I ai n't get time to eat p ` litely , '' he say when Marilla reprove him .
`` Dora ai n't half as hungry a I be .
Look at all the ex ` cise I take on the road here .
That cake 's awful nice and plummy .
We have n't have any cake at home for ever 'n ever so long , 'cause mother be too sick to make it and Mrs. Sprott say it be as much a she could do to bake our bread for u .
And Mrs. Wiggins never put any plum in HER cake .
Catch her !
Can I have another piece ? ''

However , she remind Davy that he ought to say `` Thank you '' for it .

When he have finish the slice he say , `` If you 'll give me ANOTHER piece I 'll say thank you for IT . ''

`` But do n't you want to be ? ''
say shocked Anne .

But you ca n't be a gemplum till you grow up . ''
`` Oh , indeed you can , '' Anne hasten to say , think she saw a chance to sow good seed betimes .
`` You can begin to be a gentleman when you be a little boy .
And gentleman NEVER snatch thing from lady ... or forget to say thank you ... or pull anybody 's hair . ''

`` I guess I 'll wait till I 'm grow up to be one . ''

It have be a hard day for her , what with the funeral and the long drive .
At that moment she look forward to the future with a pessimism that would have do credit to Eliza Andrews herself .
The twin be not noticeably alike , although both be fair .
Dora have long sleek curl that never get out of order .
Davy have a crop of fuzzy little yellow ringlet all over his round head .
Dora 's hazel eye be gentle and mild ; Davy 's be a roguish and dance a an elf 's .
Dora 's nose be straight , Davy 's a positive snub ; Dora have a `` prune and prism '' mouth , Davy 's be all smile ; and besides , he have a dimple in one cheek and none in the other , which give him a dear , comical , lopsided look when he laugh .
Mirth and mischief lurk in every corner of his little face .
`` They 'd better go to bed , '' say Marilla , who think it be the easy way to dispose of them .
`` Dora will sleep with me and you can put Davy in the west gable .
You 're not afraid to sleep alone , be you , Davy ? ''
`` No ; but I ai n't go to bed for ever so long yet , '' say Davy comfortably .
`` Oh , yes , you be . ''
That be all the much-tried Marilla say , but something in her tone squelch even Davy .
He trot obediently upstairs with Anne .
`` When I 'm grow up the very first thing I 'm go to do be stay up ALL night just to see what it would be like , '' he tell her confidentially .
In after year Marilla never think of that first week of the twin ' sojourn at Green Gables without a shiver .
Not that it really be so much bad than the week that follow it ; but it seem so by reason of it novelty .
There be seldom a wake minute of any day when Davy be not in mischief or devise it ; but his first notable exploit occur two day after his arrival , on Sunday morning ... a fine , warm day , a hazy and mild a September .
Anne dress him for church while Marilla attend to Dora .
Davy at first object strongly to have his face wash .
`` Marilla wash it yesterday ... and Mrs. Wiggins scour me with hard soap the day of the funeral .
That 's enough for one week .
I do n't see the good of be so awful clean .
It 's lot more comfable be dirty . ''
`` Paul Irving wash his face every day of his own accord , '' say Anne astutely .
Davy have be an inmate of Green Gables for little over forty-eight hour ; but he already worship Anne and hat Paul Irving , whom he have hear Anne praise enthusiastically the day after his arrival .
If Paul Irving wash his face every day , that settle it .
He , Davy Keith , would do it too , if it kill him .
The same consideration induce him to submit meekly to the other detail of his toilet , and he be really a handsome little lad when all be do .
Anne felt an almost maternal pride in him a she lead him into the old Cuthbert pew .
Davy behave quite well at first , be occupy in cast covert glance at all the small boy within view and wonder which be Paul Irving .
The first two hymn and the Scripture reading pass off uneventfully .
Mr. Allan be pray when the sensation come .
Lauretta White be sit in front of Davy , her head slightly bent and her fair hair hang in two long braid , between which a tempting expanse of white neck show , encase in a loose lace frill .
Lauretta be a fat , placid-looking child of eight , who have conduct herself irreproachably in church from the very first day her mother carry her there , an infant of six month .
Davy thrust his hand into his pocket and produce ... a caterpillar , a furry , squirm caterpillar .
Marilla saw and clutch at him but she be too late .
Davy drop the caterpillar down Lauretta 's neck .
Right into the middle of Mr. Allan 's prayer burst a series of pierce shriek .
The minister stop appalled and open his eye .
Every head in the congregation fly up .
Lauretta White be dance up and down in her pew , clutch frantically at the back of her dress .
`` Ow ... mommer ... mommer ... ow ... take it off ... ow ... get it out ... ow ... that bad boy put it down my neck ... ow ... mommer ... it 's go far down ... ow ... ow ... ow ... '' Mrs. White rise and with a set face carry the hysterical , writhe Lauretta out of church .
Her shriek die away in the distance and Mr. Allan proceed with the service .
But everybody felt that it be a failure that day .
For the first time in her life Marilla take no notice of the text and Anne sit with scarlet cheek of mortification .
When they get home Marilla put Davy to bed and make him stay there for the rest of the day .
She would not give him any dinner but allow him a plain tea of bread and milk .
Anne carry it to him and sit sorrowfully by him while he eat it with an unrepentant relish .
But Anne 's mournful eye trouble him .
`` I s ` pose , '' he say reflectively , `` that Paul Irving would n't have drop a caterpillar down a girl 's neck in church , would he ? ''
`` Indeed he would n't , '' say Anne sadly .
`` Well , I 'm kind of sorry I do it , then , '' concede Davy .
`` But it be such a jolly big caterpillar ... I pick him up on the church step just a we go in .
It seem a pity to waste him .
And say , be n't it fun to hear that girl yell ? ''
Tuesday afternoon the Aid Society meet at Green Gables .
Anne hurry home from school , for she know that Marilla would need all the assistance she could give .
Dora , neat and proper , in her nicely starch white dress and black sash , be sit with the member of the Aid in the parlor , speak demurely when speak to , keep silence when not , and in every way comport herself a a model child .
Davy , blissfully dirty , be make mud pie in the barnyard .
`` I tell him he might , '' say Marilla wearily .
`` I think it would keep him out of bad mischief .
He can only get dirty at that .
We 'll have our tea over before we call him to his .
Dora can have hers with u , but I would never dare to let Davy sit down at the table with all the Aids here . ''

`` No , I never will .

`` Davy Keith ! ''

IX A Question of Color `` That old nuisance of a Rachel Lynde be here again today , pester me for a subscription towards buy a carpet for the vestry room , '' say Mr. Harrison wrathfully .

`` That be always what be wrong when people do n't like each other .

X Davy in Search of a Sensation Anne , walk home from school through the Birch Path one November afternoon , felt convinced afresh that life be a very wonderful thing .

say Anne , who have never quite get over her childish habit of talk to herself .

`` Then , '' say Davy decidedly , `` Marilla be bad , for SHE tell them .
And she 's bad 'n me , for I do n't know it be wrong but she do . ''
`` Davy Keith , Marilla never tell a story in her life , '' say Anne indignantly .
`` She do so .
She tell me last Tuesday that something dreadful WOULD happen to me if I do n't say my prayer every night .
And I have n't say them for over a week , just to see what would happen ... and nothing have , '' conclude Davy in an aggrieved tone .
Anne choke back a mad desire to laugh with the conviction that it would be fatal , and then earnestly set about save Marilla 's reputation .
`` Why , Davy Keith , '' she say solemnly , `` something dreadful HAS happen to you this very day . ''
Davy look sceptical .
`` I s ` pose you mean be send to bed without any supper , '' he say scornfully , `` but THAT be n't dreadful .
Course , I do n't like it , but I 've be send to bed so much since I come here that I 'm get use to it .
And you do n't save anything by make me go without supper either , for I always eat twice as much for breakfast . ''
`` I do n't mean your be send to bed .
I mean the fact that you tell a falsehood today .
And , Davy , '' ... Anne lean over the footboard of the bed and shake her finger impressively at the culprit ... `` for a boy to tell what be n't true be almost the bad thing that could HAPPEN to him ... almost the very bad .
So you see Marilla tell you the truth . ''
`` But I think the something bad would be exciting , '' protest Davy in an injured tone .
`` Marilla be n't to blame for what you think .
Bad thing be n't always excite .
They 're very often just nasty and stupid . ''
`` It be awful funny to see Marilla and you look down the well , though , '' say Davy , hug his knee .
Anne keep a sober face until she get downstairs and then she collapse on the sit room lounge and laugh until her side ache .
`` I wish you 'd tell me the joke , '' say Marilla , a little grimly .
`` I have n't see much to laugh at today . ''
`` You 'll laugh when you hear this , '' assure Anne .
And Marilla do laugh , which show how much her education have advance since the adoption of Anne .
But she sigh immediately afterwards .
`` I suppose I should n't have tell him that , although I hear a minister say it to a child once .
But he do aggravate me so .
It be that night you be at the Carmody concert and I be put him to bed .
He say he do n't see the good of pray until he get big enough to be of some importance to God .
Anne , I do not know what we be go to do with that child .
I never saw his beat .
I 'm feel clean discourage . ''
`` Oh , do n't say that , Marilla .
Remember how bad I be when I come here . ''
`` Anne , you never be bad ... NEVER .
I see that now , when I 've learn what real badness be .
You be always get into terrible scrape , I 'll admit , but your motive be always good .
Davy be just bad from sheer love of it . ''
`` Oh , no , I do n't think it be real badness with him either , '' plead Anne .
`` It 's just mischief .
And it be rather quiet for him here , you know .
He have no other boy to play with and his mind have to have something to occupy it .
Dora be so prim and proper she be no good for a boy 's playmate .
I really think it would be good to let them go to school , Marilla . ''
`` No , '' say Marilla resolutely , `` my father always say that no child should be cooped up in the four wall of a school until it be seven year old , and Mr. Allan say the same thing .
The twin can have a few lesson at home but go to school they sha n't till they 're seven . ''
`` Well , we must try to reform Davy at home then , '' say Anne cheerfully .
`` With all his fault he 's really a dear little chap .
I ca n't help love him .
Marilla , it may be a dreadful thing to say , but honestly , I like Davy good than Dora , for all she 's so good . ''
`` I do n't know but that I do , myself , '' confess Marilla , `` and it be n't fair , for Dora be n't a bit of trouble .
There could n't be a good child and you 'd hardly know she be in the house . ''
`` Dora be too good , '' say Anne .
`` She 'd behave just as well if there be n't a soul to tell her what to do .
She be bear already bring up , so she do n't need u ; and I think , '' conclude Anne , hit on a very vital truth , `` that we always love best the people who need u .
Davy need u badly . ''
`` He certainly need something , '' agree Marilla .
`` Rachel Lynde would say it be a good spanking . ''

` Dear teacher , '' `` You say we might write about a visit .
I never visit but once .
It be at my Aunt Mary 's last winter .
My Aunt Mary be a very particular woman and a great housekeeper .
The first night I be there we be at tea .
I knock over a jug and break it .
Aunt Mary say she have have that jug ever since she be marry and nobody have ever break it before .
When we get up I step on her dress and all the gather tear out of the skirt .
The next morning when I get up I hit the pitcher against the basin and crack them both and I upset a cup of tea on the tablecloth at breakfast .
When I be help Aunt Mary with the dinner dish I drop a china plate and it smash .
That even I fell downstairs and sprain my ankle and have to stay in bed for a week .
I hear Aunt Mary tell Uncle Joseph it be a mercy or I 'd have break everything in the house .
When I get well it be time to go home .
I do n't like visit very much .
I like go to school well , especially since I come to Avonlea . ''

`` Paul 's Letter . ''
` My dear teacher , '' ` You tell u we might write you about some interesting people we know .
I think the most interesting people I know be my rock people and I mean to tell you about them .
I have never tell anybody about them except grandma and father but I would like to have you know about them because you understand thing .
There be a great many people who do not understand thing so there be no use in tell them . ' ''
` My rock people live at the shore .
I use to visit them almost every evening before the winter come .
Now I ca n't go till spring , but they will be there , for people like that never change ... that be the splendid thing about them .
Nora be the first one of them I get acquaint with and so I think I love her the best .
She live in Andrews ' Cove and she have black hair and black eye , and she know all about the mermaid and the water kelpy .
You ought to hear the story she can tell .
Then there be the Twin Sailors .
They do n't live anywhere , they sail all the time , but they often come ashore to talk to me .
They be a pair of jolly tar and they have see everything in the world ... and more than what be in the world .
Do you know what happen to the young Twin Sailor once ?
He be sail and he sail right into a moonglade .
A moonglade be the track the full moon make on the water when it be rise from the sea , you know , teacher .
Well , the young Twin Sailor sail along the moonglade till he come right up to the moon , and there be a little golden door in the moon and he open it and sail right through .
He have some wonderful adventure in the moon but it would make this letter too long to tell them . ' ''
` Then there be the Golden Lady of the cave .
One day I find a big cave down on the shore and I go away in and after a while I find the Golden Lady .
She have golden hair right down to her foot and her dress be all glittering and glisten like gold that be alive .
And she have a golden harp and play on it all day long ... you can hear the music any time along shore if you listen carefully but most people would think it be only the wind among the rock .
I 've never tell Nora about the Golden Lady .
I be afraid it might hurt her feeling .
It even hurt her feeling if I talk too long with the Twin Sailors . ' '' '
I always meet the Twin Sailors at the Striped Rocks .
The young Twin Sailor be very good-tempered but the old Twin Sailor can look dreadfully fierce at time .
I have my suspicion about that old Twin .
I believe he 'd be a pirate if he dare .
There 's really something very mysterious about him .
He swear once and I tell him if he ever do it again he need n't come ashore to talk to me because I 'd promise grandmother I 'd never associate with anybody that swore .
He be pretty well scared , I can tell you , and he say if I would forgive him he would take me to the sunset .
So the next evening when I be sit on the Striped Rocks the old Twin come sail over the sea in an enchanted boat and I get in her .
The boat be all pearly and rainbowy , like the inside of the mussel shell , and her sail be like moonshine .
Well , we sail right across to the sunset .
Think of that , teacher , I 've be in the sunset .
And what do you suppose it be ?
The sunset be a land all flower .
We sail into a great garden , and the cloud be bed of flower .
We sail into a great harbor , all the color of gold , and I step right out of the boat on a big meadow all cover with buttercup as big a rose .
I stay there for ever so long .
It seem nearly a year but the Oldest Twin say it be only a few minute .
You see , in the sunset land the time be ever so much long than it be here . ' ''
` Your loving pupil Paul Irving . ' ''
` P. S. of course , this letter be n't really true , teacher .
P.I. ' '' XII A Jonah Day It really begin the night before with a restless , wakeful vigil of grumble toothache .
When Anne arose in the dull , bitter winter morning she felt that life be flat , stale , and unprofitable .
She go to school in no angelic mood .
Her cheek be swollen and her face ache .
The schoolroom be cold and smoky , for the fire refuse to burn and the child be huddle about it in shiver group .
Anne send them to their seat with a sharp tone than she have ever use before .
Anthony Pye strut to his with his usual impertinent swagger and she saw him whisper something to his seat-mate and then glance at her with a grin .
Never , so it seem to Anne , have there be so many squeaky pencil a there be that morning ; and when Barbara Shaw come up to the desk with a sum she trip over the coal scuttle with disastrous result .
The coal roll to every part of the room , her slate be break into fragment , and when she pick herself up , her face , stain with coal dust , send the boy into roar of laughter .
Anne turn from the second reader class which she be hear .
`` Really , Barbara , '' she say icily , `` if you can not move without fall over something you 'd better remain in your seat .
It be positively disgraceful for a girl of your age to be so awkward . ''
Poor Barbara stumble back to her desk , her tear combine with the coal dust to produce an effect truly grotesque .
Never before have her beloved , sympathetic teacher spoken to her in such a tone or fashion , and Barbara be heartbroken .
Anne herself felt a prick of conscience but it only serve to increase her mental irritation , and the second reader class remember that lesson yet , as well a the unmerciful infliction of arithmetic that follow .
Just a Anne be snap the sum out St. Clair Donnell arrive breathlessly .
`` You be half an hour late , St. Clair , '' Anne remind him frigidly .
`` Why be this ? ''
`` Please , miss , I have to help ma make a pudding for dinner 'cause we 're expect company and Clarice Almira 's sick , '' be St. Clair 's answer , give in a perfectly respectful voice but nevertheless provocative of great mirth among his mate .
`` Take your seat and work out the six problem on page eighty-four of your arithmetic for punishment , '' say Anne .
St. Clair look rather amaze at her tone but he go meekly to his desk and take out his slate .
Then he stealthily pass a small parcel to Joe Sloane across the aisle .
Anne catch him in the act and jump to a fatal conclusion about that parcel .
Old Mrs. Hiram Sloane have lately take to make and sell `` nut cake '' by way of add to her scanty income .
The cake be specially tempt to small boy and for several week Anne have have not a little trouble in regard to them .
On their way to school the boy would invest their spare cash at Mrs. Hiram 's , bring the cake along with them to school , and , if possible , eat them and treat their mate during school hour .
Anne have warn them that if they bring any more cake to school they would be confiscate ; and yet here be St. Clair Donnell coolly pass a parcel of them , wrap up in the blue and white strip paper Mrs. Hiram use , under her very eyes .
`` Joseph , '' say Anne quietly , `` bring that parcel here . ''
Joe , startle and abash , obey .
He be a fat urchin who always blush and stutter when he be frighten .
Never do anybody look more guilty than poor Joe at that moment .
`` Throw it into the fire , '' say Anne .
Joe look very blank .
`` P ... p ... p ... lease , m ... m ... miss , '' he begin .
`` Do a I tell you , Joseph , without any word about it . ''
`` B ... b ... but m ... m ... miss ... th ... th ... they 're ... '' gasp Joe in desperation .
`` Joseph , be you go to obey me or be you NOT ? ''
say Anne .
A bolder and more self-possessed lad than Joe Sloane would have be overawe by her tone and the dangerous flash of her eye .
This be a new Anne whom none of her pupil have ever see before .
Joe , with an agonized glance at St. Clair , go to the stove , open the big , square front door , and throw the blue and white parcel in , before St. Clair , who have spring to his foot , could utter a word .
Then he dodge back just in time .
For a few moment the terrified occupant of Avonlea school do not know whether it be an earthquake or a volcanic explosion that have occur .
The innocent look parcel which Anne have rashly suppose to contain Mrs. Hiram 's nut cake really hold an assortment of firecracker and pinwheel for which Warren Sloane have send to town by St. Clair Donnell 's father the day before , intend to have a birthday celebration that even .
The cracker go off in a thunderclap of noise and the pinwheel burst out of the door spin madly around the room , hiss and splutter .
Anne drop into her chair white with dismay and all the girl climb shriek upon their desk .
Joe Sloane stand a one transfixed in the midst of the commotion and St. Clair , helpless with laughter , rock to and fro in the aisle .
Prillie Rogerson faint and Annetta Bell go into hysteric .
It seem a long time , although it be really only a few minute , before the last pinwheel subside .
Anne , recover herself , spring to open door and window and let out the gas and smoke which fill the room .
Then she help the girl carry the unconscious Prillie into the porch , where Barbara Shaw , in an agony of desire to be useful , pour a pailful of half frozen water over Prillie 's face and shoulder before anyone could stop her .
It be a full hour before quiet be restore ... but it be a quiet that might be felt .
Everybody realize that even the explosion have not clear the teacher 's mental atmosphere .
Nobody , except Anthony Pye , dare whisper a word .
Ned Clay accidentally squeak his pencil while work a sum , catch Anne 's eye and wish the floor would open and swallow him up .
The geography class be whisk through a continent with a speed that make them dizzy .
The grammar class be parse and analyze within an inch of their life .
Chester Sloane , spell `` odoriferous '' with two f 's , be make to feel that he could never live down the disgrace of it , either in this world or that which be to come .
Anne know that she have make herself ridiculous and that the incident would be laugh over that night at a score of tea-tables , but the knowledge only anger her further .
In a calmer mood she could have carry off the situation with a laugh but now that be impossible ; so she ignore it in icy disdain .
When Anne return to the school after dinner all the child be as usual in their seat and every face be bent studiously over a desk except Anthony Pye 's .
He peer across his book at Anne , his black eye sparkle with curiosity and mockery .
Anne twitch open the drawer of her desk in search of chalk and under her very hand a lively mouse spring out of the drawer , scamper over the desk , and leap to the floor .
Anne scream and spring back , a if it have be a snake , and Anthony Pye laugh aloud .
Then a silence fell ... a very creepy , uncomfortable silence .
Annetta Bell be of two mind whether to go into hysteric again or not , especially a she do n't know just where the mouse have go .
But she decide not to .
Who could take any comfort out of hysteric with a teacher so white-faced and so blazing-eyed standing before one ?
`` Who put that mouse in my desk ? ''
say Anne .
Her voice be quite low but it make a shiver go up and down Paul Irving 's spine .
Joe Sloane catch her eye , felt responsible from the crown of his head to the sole of his foot , but stutter out wildly , `` N ... n ... not m ... m ... me t ... t ... teacher , n ... n ... not m ... m ... me . ''
Anne pay no attention to the wretched Joseph .
She look at Anthony Pye , and Anthony Pye look back unabashed and unashamed .
`` Anthony , be it you ? ''
`` Yes , it be , '' say Anthony insolently .
Anne take her pointer from her desk .
It be a long , heavy hardwood pointer .
`` Come here , Anthony . ''
It be far from be the most severe punishment Anthony Pye have ever undergone .
Anne , even the stormy-souled Anne she be at that moment , could not have punish any child cruelly .
But the pointer nip keenly and finally Anthony 's bravado fail him ; he wince and the tear come to his eye .
Anne , conscience-stricken , drop the pointer and tell Anthony to go to his seat .
She sit down at her desk feeling ashamed , repentant , and bitterly mortify .
Her quick anger be go and she would have give much to have be able to seek relief in tear .
So all her boast have come to this ... she have actually whip one of her pupil .
How Jane would triumph !
And how Mr. Harrison would chuckle !
But bad than this , bitter thought of all , she have lose her last chance of win Anthony Pye .
Never would he like her now .
Anne , by what somebody have call `` a Herculaneum effort , '' keep back her tear until she get home that night .
Then she shut herself in the east gable room and wept all her shame and remorse and disappointment into her pillow ... weep so long that Marilla grow alarm , invade the room , and insist on know what the trouble be .
`` The trouble be , I 've get thing the matter with my conscience , '' sob Anne .
`` Oh , this have be such a Jonah day , Marilla .
I 'm so ashamed of myself .
I lose my temper and whip Anthony Pye . ''
`` I 'm glad to hear it , '' say Marilla with decision .
`` It 's what you should have do long ago . ''
`` Oh , no , no , Marilla .
And I do n't see how I can ever look those child in the face again .
I feel that I have humiliate myself to the very dust .
You do n't know how cross and hateful and horrid I be .
I ca n't forget the expression in Paul Irving 's eye ... he look so surprised and disappointed .
Oh , Marilla , I HAVE try so hard to be patient and to win Anthony 's liking ... and now it have all go for nothing . ''
Marilla pass her hard work-worn hand over the girl 's glossy , tumble hair with a wonderful tenderness .
When Anne 's sob grow quiet she say , very gently for her , `` You take thing too much to heart , Anne .
We all make mistake ... but people forget them .
And Jonah day come to everybody .
As for Anthony Pye , why need you care if he do dislike you ?
He be the only one . ''
`` I ca n't help it .
I want everybody to love me and it hurt me so when anybody do n't .
And Anthony never will now .
Oh , I just make an idiot of myself today , Marilla .
I 'll tell you the whole story . ''
Marilla listen to the whole story , and if she smile at certain part of it Anne never know .
When the tale be end she say briskly , `` Well , never mind .
This day 's do and there 's a new one come tomorrow , with no mistake in it yet , a you use to say yourself .
Just come downstairs and have your supper .
You 'll see if a good cup of tea and those plum puff I make today wo n't hearten you up . ''
`` Plum puff wo n't minister to a mind diseased , '' say Anne disconsolately ; but Marilla think it a good sign that she have recover sufficiently to adapt a quotation .
The cheerful supper table , with the twin ' bright face , and Marilla 's matchless plum puff ... of which Davy ate four ... do `` hearten her up '' considerably after all .
She have a good sleep that night and awaken in the morning to find herself and the world transform .
It have snow softly and thickly all through the hour of darkness and the beautiful whiteness , glitter in the frosty sunshine , look like a mantle of charity cast over all the mistake and humiliation of the past .
`` Every morn be a fresh beginning , Every morn be the world make new , '' sing Anne , a she dress .
Owing to the snow she have to go around by the road to school and she think it be certainly an impish coincidence that Anthony Pye should come plough along just a she leave the Green Gables lane .
She felt as guilty a if their position be reverse ; but to her unspeakable astonishment Anthony not only lift his cap ... which he have never do before ... but say easily , `` Kind of bad walking , ai n't it ?
Can I take those book for you , teacher ? ''
Anne surrender her book and wonder if she could possibly be awake .
Anthony walk on in silence to the school , but when Anne take her book she smile down at him ... not the stereotype `` kind '' smile she have so persistently assume for his benefit but a sudden outflashing of good comradeship .
Anthony smile ... no , if the truth must be tell , Anthony GRINNED back .
A grin be not generally suppose to be a respectful thing ; yet Anne suddenly felt that if she have not yet win Anthony 's liking she have , somehow or other , win his respect .
Mrs. Rachel Lynde come up the next Saturday and confirm this .
`` Well , Anne , I guess you 've win over Anthony Pye , that 's what .
He say he believe you be some good after all , even if you be a girl .
Says that whip you give him be ` just as good a a man 's . ' ''
`` I never expect to win him by whip him , though , '' say Anne , a little mournfully , feel that her ideal have play her false somewhere .
`` It do n't seem right .
I 'm sure my theory of kindness ca n't be wrong . ''
`` No , but the Pyes be an exception to every know rule , that 's what , '' declare Mrs. Rachel with conviction .
Mr. Harrison say , `` Thought you 'd come to it , '' when he hear it , and Jane rub it in rather unmercifully .
XIII A Golden Picnic Anne , on her way to Orchard Slope , meet Diana , bound for Green Gables , just where the mossy old log bridge span the brook below the Haunted Wood , and they sit down by the margin of the Dryad 's Bubble , where tiny fern be unroll like curly-headed green pixy folk waken up from a nap .
`` I be just on my way over to invite you to help me celebrate my birthday on Saturday , '' say Anne .
`` Your birthday ?
But your birthday be in March ! ''
`` That be n't my fault , '' laugh Anne .
`` If my parent have consult me it would never have happen then .
I should have choose to be bear in spring , of course .
It must be delightful to come into the world with the mayflower and violet .
You would always feel that you be their foster sister .
But since I do n't , the next best thing be to celebrate my birthday in the spring .
Priscilla be come over Saturday and Jane will be home .
We 'll all four start off to the wood and spend a golden day make the acquaintance of the spring .
We none of u really know her yet , but we 'll meet her back there a we never can anywhere else .
I want to explore all those field and lonely place anyhow .
I have a conviction that there be score of beautiful nook there that have never really be SEEN although they may have be LOOKED at .
We 'll make friend with wind and sky and sun , and bring home the spring in our heart . ''

`` But wo n't it be very damp in some place yet ? ''
`` Oh , we 'll wear rubber , '' be Anne 's concession to practicality .
`` And I want you to come over early Saturday morning and help me prepare lunch .
I 'm go to have the dainty thing possible ... thing that will match the spring , you understand ... little jelly tart and lady finger , and drop cooky frost with pink and yellow icing , and buttercup cake .
And we must have sandwich too , though they 're NOT very poetical . ''
Saturday prove an ideal day for a picnic ... a day of breeze and blue , warm , sunny , with a little rollicking wind blow across meadow and orchard .
Over every sunlit upland and field be a delicate , flower-starred green .
Mr. Harrison , harrow at the back of his farm and feel some of the spring witch-work even in his sober , middle-aged blood , saw four girl , basket laden , trip across the end of his field where it join a fringing woodland of birch and fir .
Their blithe voice and laughter echo down to him .
`` It 's so easy to be happy on a day like this , be n't it ? ''
Anne be say , with true Anneish philosophy .
`` Let 's try to make this a really golden day , girl , a day to which we can always look back with delight .
We 're to seek for beauty and refuse to see anything else .
` Begone , dull care ! '
Jane , you be think of something that go wrong in school yesterday . ''
`` How do you know ? ''
gasp Jane , amaze .
`` Oh , I know the expression ... I 've felt it often enough on my own face .
But put it out of your mind , there 's a dear .
It will keep till Monday ... or if it do n't so much the good .

There 's something for memory 's picture gallery .

That 's the first good gift our day have give u . ''
`` If a kiss could be see I think it would look like a violet , '' say Priscilla .
Anne glow .
`` I 'm so glad you SPOKE that thought , Priscilla , instead of just think it and keep it to yourself .
This world would be a much more interesting place ... although it IS very interesting anyhow ... if people speak out their real thought . ''
`` It would be too hot to hold some folk , '' quote Jane sagely .
`` I suppose it might be , but that would be their own fault for think nasty thing .
Anyhow , we can tell all our thought today because we be go to have nothing but beautiful thought .
Everybody can say just what come into her head .
THAT be conversation .
Here 's a little path I never saw before .
Let 's explore it . ''
The path be a wind one , so narrow that the girl walk in single file and even then the fir bough brush their face .
Under the fir be velvety cushion of moss , and far on , where the tree be small and few , the ground be rich in a variety of green grow thing .
`` What a lot of elephant 's ear , '' exclaim Diana .
`` I 'm go to pick a big bunch , they 're so pretty . ''
`` How do such graceful feathery thing ever come to have such a dreadful name ? ''
ask Priscilla .
`` Because the person who first name them either have no imagination at all or else far too much , '' say Anne , `` Oh , girl , look at that ! ''
`` That '' be a shallow woodland pool in the center of a little open glade where the path end .
Later on in the season it would be dry up and it place fill with a rank growth of fern ; but now it be a glimmering placid sheet , round a a saucer and clear a crystal .
A ring of slender young birch encircle it and little fern fringe it margin .
`` HOW sweet ! ''
say Jane .
`` Let u dance around it like wood-nymphs , '' cry Anne , drop her basket and extend her hand .
But the dance be not a success for the ground be boggy and Jane 's rubber come off .
`` You ca n't be a wood-nymph if you have to wear rubber , '' be her decision .
`` Well , we must name this place before we leave it , '' say Anne , yield to the indisputable logic of fact .
`` Everybody suggest a name and we 'll draw lot .
Diana ? ''
`` Birch Pool , '' suggest Diana promptly .
`` Crystal Lake , '' say Jane .
Anne , stand behind them , implore Priscilla with her eye not to perpetrate another such name and Priscilla rise to the occasion with `` Glimmer-glass . ''
Anne 's selection be `` The Fairies ' Mirror . ''
The name be write on strip of birch bark with a pencil Schoolma'am Jane produce from her pocket , and place in Anne 's hat .
Then Priscilla shut her eye and draw one .
`` Crystal Lake , '' read Jane triumphantly .
Crystal Lake it be , and if Anne think that chance have play the pool a shabby trick she do not say so .
Pushing through the undergrowth beyond , the girl come out to the young green seclusion of Mr. Silas Sloane 's back pasture .
Across it they find the entrance to a lane strike up through the wood and vote to explore it also .
It reward their quest with a succession of pretty surprise .
First , skirt Mr. Sloane 's pasture , come an archway of wild cherry tree all in bloom .
The girl swing their hat on their arm and wreathe their hair with the creamy , fluffy blossom .
Then the lane turn at right angle and plunge into a spruce wood so thick and dark that they walk in a gloom a of twilight , with not a glimpse of sky or sunlight to be see .
`` This be where the bad wood elf dwell , '' whisper Anne .
`` They be impish and malicious but they ca n't harm u , because they be not allow to do evil in the spring .
There be one peeping at u around that old twisted fir ; and do n't you see a group of them on that big freckly toadstool we just pass ?
The good fairy always dwell in the sunshiny place . ''
`` I wish there really be fairy , '' say Jane .
`` Would n't it be nice to have three wish grant you ... or even only one ?
What would you wish for , girl , if you could have a wish grant ?
I 'd wish to be rich and beautiful and clever . ''
`` I 'd wish to be tall and slender , '' say Diana .
`` I would wish to be famous , '' say Priscilla .
Anne thought of her hair and then dismiss the thought a unworthy .
`` I 'd wish it might be spring all the time and in everybody 's heart and all our life , '' she say .
`` But that , '' say Priscilla , `` would be just wish this world be like heaven . ''
`` Only like a part of heaven .
In the other part there would be summer and autumn ... yes , and a bit of winter , too .
I think I want glitter snowy field and white frost in heaven sometimes .
Do n't you , Jane ? ''

Jane be a good girl , a member of the church , who try conscientiously to live up to her profession and believe everything she have be teach .

ask Anne .

I tell her we would n't be think of dress at all there . ''

I believe we 'll all wear beautiful dress ... or I suppose RAIMENT would be a more suitable way of speaking .
I shall want to wear pink for a few century at first ... it would take me that long to get tire of it , I feel sure .
I do love pink so and I can never wear it in THIS world . ''
Past the spruce the lane dip down into a sunny little open where a log bridge span a brook ; and then come the glory of a sunlit beechwood where the air be like transparent golden wine , and the leaf fresh and green , and the wood floor a mosaic of tremulous sunshine .
Then more wild cherry , and a little valley of lissome fir , and then a hill so steep that the girl lose their breath climb it ; but when they reach the top and come out into the open the pretty surprise of all await them .
Beyond be the `` back field '' of the farm that run out to the upper Carmody road .
Just before them , hem in by beech and fir but open to the south , be a little corner and in it a garden ... or what have once be a garden .
A tumbledown stone dyke , overgrown with moss and grass , surround it .
Along the eastern side run a row of garden cherry tree , white a a snowdrift .
There be trace of old path still and a double line of rosebush through the middle ; but all the rest of the space be a sheet of yellow and white narcissus , in their airy , most lavish , wind-swayed bloom above the lush green grass .
`` Oh , how perfectly lovely ! ''
three of the girl cry .
Anne only gaze in eloquent silence .
`` How in the world do it happen that there ever be a garden back here ? ''
say Priscilla in amazement .
`` It must be Hester Gray 's garden , '' say Diana .
`` I 've hear mother speak of it but I never saw it before , and I would n't have suppose that it could be in existence still .
You 've hear the story , Anne ? ''
`` No , but the name seem familiar to me . ''
`` Oh , you 've see it in the graveyard .
She be bury down there in the poplar corner .
You know the little brown stone with the opening gate carve on it and ` Sacred to the memory of Hester Gray , age twenty-two . '
Jordan Gray be bury right beside her but there 's no stone to him .
It 's a wonder Marilla never tell you about it , Anne .
To be sure , it happen thirty year ago and everybody have forget . ''
`` Well , if there 's a story we must have it , '' say Anne .
`` Let 's sit right down here among the narcissus and Diana will tell it .
Why , girl , there be hundred of them ... they 've spread over everything .
It look a if the garden be carpet with moonshine and sunshine combine .
This be a discovery worth making .
To think that I 've live within a mile of this place for six year and have never see it before !
Now , Diana . ''
`` Long ago , '' begin Diana , `` this farm belong to old Mr. David Gray .
He do n't live on it ... he live where Silas Sloane live now .
He have one son , Jordan , and he go up to Boston one winter to work and while he be there he fell in love with a girl name Hester Murray .
She be work in a store and she hat it .
She 'd be bring up in the country and she always want to get back .
When Jordan ask her to marry him she say she would if he 'd take her away to some quiet spot where she 'd see nothing but field and tree .
So he bring her to Avonlea .
Mrs. Lynde say he be take a fearful risk in marry a Yankee , and it 's certain that Hester be very delicate and a very poor housekeeper ; but mother say she be very pretty and sweet and Jordan just worship the ground she walk on .
Well , Mr. Gray give Jordan this farm and he build a little house back here and Jordan and Hester live in it for four year .
She never go out much and hardly anybody go to see her except mother and Mrs. Lynde .
Jordan make her this garden and she be crazy about it and spend most of her time in it .
She be n't much of a housekeeper but she have a knack with flower .
And then she get sick .
Mother say she think she be in consumption before she ever come here .
She never really lay up but just grow weak and weak all the time .
Jordan would n't have anybody to wait on her .
He do it all himself and mother say he be a tender and gentle a a woman .
Every day he 'd wrap her in a shawl and carry her out to the garden and she 'd lie there on a bench quite happy .
They say she use to make Jordan kneel down by her every night and morning and pray with her that she might die out in the garden when the time come .
And her prayer be answer .
One day Jordan carry her out to the bench and then he pick all the rose that be out and heap them over her ; and she just smile up at him ... and close her eye ... and that , '' conclude Diana softly , `` be the end . ''
`` Oh , what a dear story , '' sigh Anne , wipe away her tear .
`` What become of Jordan ? ''
ask Priscilla .
`` He sell the farm after Hester die and go back to Boston .
Mr. Jabez Sloane buy the farm and haul the little house out to the road .
Jordan die about ten year after and he be bring home and bury beside Hester . ''
`` I ca n't understand how she could have want to live back here , away from everything , '' say Jane .
`` Oh , I can easily understand THAT , '' say Anne thoughtfully .
`` I would n't want it myself for a steady thing , because , although I love the field and wood , I love people too .
But I can understand it in Hester .
She be tire to death of the noise of the big city and the crowd of people always come and go and care nothing for her .
She just want to escape from it all to some still , green , friendly place where she could rest .
And she get just what she want , which be something very few people do , I believe .
She have four beautiful year before she die ... four year of perfect happiness , so I think she be to be envy more than pity .
And then to shut your eye and fall asleep among rose , with the one you love best on earth smile down at you ... oh , I think it be beautiful ! ''
`` She set out those cherry tree over there , '' say Diana .
`` She tell mother she 'd never live to eat their fruit , but she want to think that something she have plant would go on living and help to make the world beautiful after she be dead . ''
`` I 'm so glad we come this way , '' say Anne , the shining-eyed .
`` This be my adopted birthday , you know , and this garden and it story be the birthday gift it have give me .
