CHAPTER I. Mrs. Rachel Lynde be Surprised Mrs. Rachel Lynde live just where the Avonlea main road dip down into a little hollow , fringe with alder and lady ' eardrop and traverse by a brook that have it source away back in the wood of the old Cuthbert place ; it be repute to be an intricate , headlong brook in it early course through those wood , with dark secret of pool and cascade ; but by the time it reach Lynde 's Hollow it be a quiet , well-conducted little stream , for not even a brook could run past Mrs. Rachel Lynde 's door without due regard for decency and decorum ; it probably be conscious that Mrs. Rachel be sit at her window , keep a sharp eye on everything that pass , from brook and child up , and that if she notice anything odd or out of place she would never rest until she have ferret out the why and wherefores thereof .
There be plenty of people in Avonlea and out of it , who can attend closely to their neighbor 's business by dint of neglect their own ; but Mrs. Rachel Lynde be one of those capable creature who can manage their own concern and those of other folk into the bargain .
She be a notable housewife ; her work be always do and well do ; she `` run '' the Sewing Circle , help run the Sunday-school , and be the strong prop of the Church Aid Society and Foreign Missions Auxiliary .
Yet with all this Mrs. Rachel find abundant time to sit for hour at her kitchen window , knit `` cotton warp '' quilt -- she have knit sixteen of them , a Avonlea housekeeper be wont to tell in awed voice -- and keep a sharp eye on the main road that cross the hollow and wind up the steep red hill beyond .
Since Avonlea occupy a little triangular peninsula jut out into the Gulf of St. Lawrence with water on two side of it , anybody who go out of it or into it have to pass over that hill road and so run the unseen gauntlet of Mrs. Rachel 's all-seeing eye .
She be sit there one afternoon in early June .
The sun be come in at the window warm and bright ; the orchard on the slope below the house be in a bridal flush of pinky-white bloom , hum over by a myriad of bee .
Thomas Lynde -- a meek little man whom Avonlea people call `` Rachel Lynde 's husband '' -- be sow his late turnip seed on the hill field beyond the barn ; and Matthew Cuthbert ought to have be sow his on the big red brook field away over by Green Gables .
Mrs. Rachel know that he ought because she have hear him tell Peter Morrison the evening before in William J. Blair 's store over at Carmody that he mean to sow his turnip seed the next afternoon .
Peter have ask him , of course , for Matthew Cuthbert have never be know to volunteer information about anything in his whole life .
And yet here be Matthew Cuthbert , at half-past three on the afternoon of a busy day , placidly drive over the hollow and up the hill ; moreover , he wear a white collar and his best suit of clothes , which be plain proof that he be go out of Avonlea ; and he have the buggy and the sorrel mare , which betoken that he be go a considerable distance .
Now , where be Matthew Cuthbert go and why be he go there ?
Had it be any other man in Avonlea , Mrs. Rachel , deftly put this and that together , might have give a pretty good guess a to both question .
But Matthew so rarely go from home that it must be something press and unusual which be take him ; he be the shy man alive and hat to have to go among stranger or to any place where he might have to talk .
Matthew , dress up with a white collar and driving in a buggy , be something that do n't happen often .
Mrs. Rachel , ponder a she might , could make nothing of it and her afternoon 's enjoyment be spoil .
`` I 'll just step over to Green Gables after tea and find out from Marilla where he 's go and why , '' the worthy woman finally conclude .
`` He do n't generally go to town this time of year and he NEVER visit ; if he 'd run out of turnip seed he would n't dress up and take the buggy to go for more ; he be n't drive fast enough to be go for a doctor .
Yet something must have happen since last night to start him off .
I 'm clean puzzle , that 's what , and I wo n't know a minute 's peace of mind or conscience until I know what have take Matthew Cuthbert out of Avonlea today . ''
Accordingly after tea Mrs. Rachel set out ; she have not far to go ; the big , ramble , orchard-embowered house where the Cuthberts live be a scant quarter of a mile up the road from Lynde 's Hollow .
To be sure , the long lane make it a good deal far .
Matthew Cuthbert 's father , a shy and silent a his son after him , have get a far away a he possibly could from his fellow men without actually retreat into the wood when he found his homestead .
